<h2 id="anchor-5">5. <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/udemy-learn-crystal-programming-125878" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Learn Crystal Programming (Timnan Sheni)</a></h2>
<p><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85687" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/5.-Learn-Crystal-Programming-Timnan-Sheni.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/5.-Learn-Crystal-Programming-Timnan-Sheni.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/5.-Learn-Crystal-Programming-Timnan-Sheni-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/5.-Learn-Crystal-Programming-Timnan-Sheni-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></p>
<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/udemy-learn-crystal-programming-125878" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Learn Crystal Programming</a> is another great project-based introductory course to the Crystal programming language. Unlike the third course in this ranking however, this <b>paid </b>course by Timnan Sheni is friendly towards absolute beginners.</p>
<p>You’ll learn how to write powerful, efficient, and concise programs in Crystal through four hands-on projects: a name guessing game; a rock, paper, scissors game; a simple calculator application; and lastly, an automatic file organizer.</p>
<p>No prior programming experience is required to take this course!</p>
<h3>What You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>You’ll start off this course by installing Crystal as well as its relevant extensions on VSCode to get the tooling out of the way.</p>
<p>Next, you’ll explore Crystal’s data types, which are very much similar to Ruby’s with types such as Strings, Numbers, Floats, and data structures like Arrays and Hashes. You’ll focus on handling user input and then making decisions based on that by using control flow.</p>
<p>“What is control flow?”, I hear you ask. Control flow consists of conditional statements such as if statements and loops such as while and unless loops that help the program choose between code paths or repeat blocks of code respectively. Armed with these concepts, you’ll create a name guessing game (similar to hangman) and use nested logic to play rock, paper, scissors.</p>
<p>The kind of programming you’ve just done is called imperative programming, where instructions are written step-by-step to perform a task. But there’s a more powerful programming paradigm called object-oriented programming, where instead of giving step-by-step instructions, you create &#8220;objects&#8221; that represent things or ideas in your program. Each object has its own properties (like name or color), can perform actions (like move or change color), and can even interact with each other. You’ll make great use of these concepts when you develop a calculator app, before finally ending the course with a IO-intensive app that organizes files into folders based on their file format.</p>
<h3>How You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>This course is 3 hours long. You’ll learn by watching the lecture videos and gaining hands-on experience by building various projects.</p>

</ul>

<h2 id="anchor-6">6. <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/exercism-crystal-110580" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Crystal (Exercism)</a></h2>
<p><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85688" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/6.-Crystal-Exercism.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/6.-Crystal-Exercism.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/6.-Crystal-Exercism-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/6.-Crystal-Exercism-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></p>
<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/exercism-crystal-110580" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Exercism is an open-source, online platform</a> for learning and practicing programming. They provide a collection of <b>free</b> coding exercises in difficulties, from easy to hard, in various programming languages (including Crystal!).</p>
<p>When I want to learn a programming language, I use Exercism to complement my learning experience. Not only does it allow me to practice what I&#8217;ve learned, but it also gives me the opportunity to compare my solutions with others. And that’s not all — the best part about Exercism is that it offers <b>free</b> mentoring.</p>
<p>I can submit my lousy code for any exercise, and after some time, receive constructive feedback from an experienced developer. This helps me improve my coding skills and write less lousier code. And so can you!</p>
<h3>What You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>Exercism offers Crystal exercises of varying difficulty levels, of which there are easy and medium exercises.</p>
<p>Examples of easy exercises include reporting leap years, converting binary numbers to their denary equivalent, and encrypting/decrypting ciphers such as Atbash, Caesar, or rational.</p>
<p>Some medium difficulty tasks are as follows: determining if a number is mathematically perfect, abundant, or deficient, calculating a person’s allergy score, and generating proverbs from a list of words.</p>
<h3>How You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>This course is self-paced, so you can take all the time you need to complete the 55+ hands-on programming exercises. Each exercise comes with automatic feedback of your code as well as personal mentoring to help you understand your code’s strengths and flaws.</p>

<h2 id="anchor-7">7. <a href="https://github.com/ilmanzo/crystal-koans" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Crystal Koans (Andrea Manzini)</a></h2>
<p><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85689" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/7.-Crystal-Koans-Andrea-Manzini.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/7.-Crystal-Koans-Andrea-Manzini.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/7.-Crystal-Koans-Andrea-Manzini-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/7.-Crystal-Koans-Andrea-Manzini-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></p>
<p><a href="https://github.com/ilmanzo/crystal-koans" target="_blank" rel="noopener">The Crystal Language Koans</a> are a set of <b>free</b> exercises aimed at teaching you the basics (and more!) of Crystal. It&#8217;s an interactive learning tool that’ll guide you through a series of challenges through trial-and-error unit testing, incrementally building your Crystal programming skills.</p>
<p>This course is much more structured than the previous course, dealing with a much wider variety of Crystal topics, including syntax, data structures, control structures, object-oriented programming, web programming, and more. The goal is to provide an engaging and hands-on way of learning the language while also reinforcing key concepts.</p>
<p>You should have some prior experience with Crystal in order to take this course.</p>
<h3>What You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>The sub-bullets (in italic) in the list show what exercises are part of that topic.</p>
<ul>
<li aria-level="1">Data types and data structures: The building blocks of every program, you’ll need them for correctness and efficiency.
<ul>
<li aria-level="2"><em>booleans, numbers, strings, symbols, nil, enums, arrays, tuples, named_tuples, sets, hashes, ranges.</em></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li aria-level="1">Control structure and functions: These allow the program to make and repeat decisions, promoting code reuse.
<ul>
<li aria-level="2"><em>loops, blocks, functions, splat.</em></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li aria-level="1">Object-Oriented Programming: Learn how to organize software around object, which have data and behavior.
<ul>
<li aria-level="2"><em>structs, classes, chaining_methods</em></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li aria-level="1">Type System: Explore Crystal’s robust type system in detail.
<ul>
<li aria-level="2"><em>generics, type_reflection</em></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li aria-level="1">Error Handling: Errors are bound to happen in run-time. Learn how to deal with them.
<ul>
<li aria-level="2"><em>exceptions</em></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li aria-level="1">Concurrency: Crystal is built for concurrency, with constructs such as channels.
<ul>
<li aria-level="2"><em>concurrency</em>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li aria-level="1">Macros: Just like Ruby, Crystal has macros. Unlike Ruby though, they expand at compile time.
<ul>
<li aria-level="2"><em>macros, macro_hooks</em></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li aria-level="1">Interoperability: Crystal prides itself on C interoperability.
<ul>
<li aria-level="2"><em>c_interop, low_level_primitives</em></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li aria-level="1">Specialized Data Types: Sometimes regular data types don’t cut it. Fortunately, Crystal is more than regular.
<ul>
<li aria-level="2"><em>bitarray, bigint, bigdecimal, static_array, complex_numbers, random</em></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li aria-level="1">Text Processing: Text can be hard. Learn how Crystal makes string operations easy.
<ul>
<li aria-level="2"><em>regular_expressions, levenshtein, semantic_version</em></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li aria-level="1">Environment &amp; Paths: Need to access files on the system? No worries!
<ul>
<li aria-level="2"><em>require_path, env, dir, path</em></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li aria-level="1">Data Formats: There perhaps may be as many data formats as there are trees on Earth. Learn how to read the most common ones.
<ul>
<li aria-level="2"><em>html, json_plain, json_custom, csv, xml, yaml</em></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li aria-level="1">HTTP &amp; Networking: Experience what Crystal is built for — efficient server processing.
<ul>
<li aria-level="2"><em>http_server, ecr</em></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3>How You’ll Learn</h3>
<p>This course consists of 51 Koans or exercises. You’ll learn through iterative testing — see the tests fail, and fill in the codes until all of the tests pass. Then, you’ll do it again until you finish all sets of exercises.</p>

		<title>The Business of Online Education: A Deep Dive Into Coursera&#8217;s Financials</title>
		<link>https://www.classcentral.com/report/coursera-economics/</link>
					<comments>https://www.classcentral.com/report/coursera-economics/#comments</comments>
		
		<dc:creator><![CDATA[Dhawal Shah]]></dc:creator>
		<pubDate>Mon, 13 Mar 2023 12:54:37 +0000</pubDate>
				<category><![CDATA[Analysis]]></category>
		<category><![CDATA[Coursera]]></category>
		<guid isPermaLink="false">https://www.classcentral.com/report/?p=85667</guid>

					<description><![CDATA[<p>Discover how Coursera makes money, its different segments, revenue growth, margins, and more.</p>
<p>The post <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/coursera-economics/">The Business of Online Education: A Deep Dive Into Coursera&#8217;s Financials</a> appeared first on <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.classcentral.com/report">The Report by Class Central</a>.</p>
]]></description>
										<content:encoded><![CDATA[<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-quarterly-revenue-2019-2022.png"><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85668" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-quarterly-revenue-2019-2022.png" alt="Coursera: Quarterly Revenue" width="1250" height="768" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-quarterly-revenue-2019-2022.png 1250w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-quarterly-revenue-2019-2022-300x184.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-quarterly-revenue-2019-2022-1024x629.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-quarterly-revenue-2019-2022-768x472.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1250px) 100vw, 1250px" /></a></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;"><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/provider/coursera">Coursera</a> started out as a noble experiment: offering free courses from top universities to anyone with an internet connection. But free courses don’t pay the bills, so Coursera had to figure out how to make money from its millions of learners.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The company tried various things over the years: limiting free access, charging for certificates, selling subscriptions, partnering with companies and governments, creating degrees and credentials…</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Now, Coursera is a big business with more than half a billion in annual revenue. I’ve previously written about </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/coursera-monetization-revenues/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">how Coursera got to this point</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">But where does its money come from? How much does it earn? How profitable is it? I have dug into Coursera’s financials, using its public filings and earnings calls. Read on to learn more.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">You can find <a href="http://classcentral.com">Class Central</a>’s entire coverage of </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/tag/coursera/'"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Coursera on The Report here</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></p>
<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/PXL_20210306_220609927-scaled.jpg"><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-74684" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/PXL_20210306_220609927-scaled.jpg" alt="Reading Coursera's S-1 at the park" width="2560" height="1920" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/PXL_20210306_220609927-scaled.jpg 2560w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/PXL_20210306_220609927-300x225.jpg 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/PXL_20210306_220609927-1024x768.jpg 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/PXL_20210306_220609927-768x576.jpg 768w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/PXL_20210306_220609927-1536x1152.jpg 1536w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/PXL_20210306_220609927-2048x1536.jpg 2048w" sizes="(max-width: 2560px) 100vw, 2560px" /></a></p>
<h2><span style="font-weight: 400;">Quick Coursera Statistics</span></h2>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Before going in depth, here are some quick stats about Coursera.</span></p>
<ul>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><b>$524M</b><span style="font-weight: 400;"> in revenue in 2022, at a loss of </span><b>$175.4M</b><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><b>47%</b><span style="font-weight: 400;"> of revenue came from learners outside of the U.S.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><b>60%</b><span style="font-weight: 400;"> of the 2022 Consumer segment revenue came from individual learners who were registered on Coursera as of December 31, 2021.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><b>118M</b><span style="font-weight: 400;"> total registered learners.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">At the end of 2022, </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/coursera-layoffs/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">in spite of layoffs</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, Coursera grew to </span><b>1,401</b><span style="font-weight: 400;"> full-time employees from </span><b>1,138</b><span style="font-weight: 400;"> the previous year.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Before the pandemic, Coursera Consumer’s growth rate was </span><b>12.6%,</b><span style="font-weight: 400;"> down from </span><b>25.4%</b><span style="font-weight: 400;"> a year earlier. In 2020, during the pandemic, it grew by </span><b>59.5%</b><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><b>30%</b><span style="font-weight: 400;"> of revenue comes from the content and credentialing programs of five partners. In 2022, this amounts to </span><b>$157M</b><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1">Class Central estimates that <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/coursera-google-new-deal/">Google’s content generates <b>$100M</b> in revenues </a>for Coursera.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span style="font-weight: 400;">How Coursera Makes Money: A Product at Every Price</span></h2>
<figure id="attachment_85669" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-85669" style="width: 1200px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-offering-structure.png"><img loading="lazy" class="wp-image-85669 size-full" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-offering-structure.png" alt="" width="1200" height="674" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-offering-structure.png 1200w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-offering-structure-300x169.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-offering-structure-1024x575.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-offering-structure-768x431.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1200px) 100vw, 1200px" /></a><figcaption id="caption-attachment-85669" class="wp-caption-text">Coursera offerings stack (<a href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://s27.q4cdn.com/928340662/files/doc_financials/2022/q4/COUR_Presentation_Q4-2022.pdf&amp;sa=D&amp;source=docs&amp;ust=1678701173929889&amp;usg=AOvVaw08uYa1FbYbpe2i0VVDKjr3">Source</a>)</figcaption></figure>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Coursera&#8217;s investor presentation includes a nice little image to showcase their catalog of products — with tiers ranging from $10 project to $45k online degrees. In 2020, Coursera introduced a catalog subscription called </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/coursera-plus-launch/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Coursera Plus</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> which gives access to a majority of the provider’s middle tiers (courses and some microcredentials) for $399 a year or $59 per month.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Five years ago, I described this strategy in </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/six-tiers-mooc-monetization/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Six Tiers of MOOC Monetization</span></a> as follows:</p>
<div class="quote relative padding-horz-large xlarge-up-padding-horz-xxlarge padding-vert-xxsmall margin-bottom-large quote-pull quote-text">
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Courses produced by brand-name institutions (now including some corporate entities in addition to universities) remain at the heart of what the MOOC platforms offer.  Additional features (e.g. credentials, additional services) are layered on top of the courses. Each tier of pricing adds some value on the tiers below. Essentially, the same product (the one that anyone can register for, free of charge) is being monetized at different pricing levels, with the free product acting as a marketing channel that feeds customers into other, higher priced products.</span><span class="quote_deco absolute top left height-100"> </span></p>
</div>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Now we can see it fully played out. Coursera calls it the “freemium flywheel”. </span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Learners can audit most of </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/coursera-free-online-courses/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Coursera’s courses for free</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, but they usually need to upgrade to get certificates and graded assignments. They can buy a single course, subscribe to a specialization, or subscribe to almost the whole catalog. The options depend on the course.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Guided Projects are the result of Coursera’s 2019 $10-million</span> <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/coursera-news-roundup/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">acquisition of Rhyme</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, an edtech startup based in Sofia, Bulgaria. Guided Projects are created by “subject matter experts” and cost $9.99. </span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Coursera’s divides its business into three different segments:</span></p>
<ul>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">The Consumer segment targets individual learners.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">The Enterprise segment is focused on serving businesses, governmental organizations, and academic institutions.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">The Degrees segment partners with universities to deliver fully online bachelor’s and master’s degrees.</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The Consumer segment generates most of Coursera’s revenue (56% of the total), but the Enterprise segment is growing faster. In the Enterprise segment, organizations and governments can buy access to most of Coursera’s catalog for their employees.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In my report for Class Central, I described how these segments started and evolved during </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/coursera-monetization-revenues/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Coursera’s monetization journey</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></p>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In 2022, Coursera&#8217;s revenues increased by 26% year-over-year from $415.3 million to $524 million, while losses grew from $145.2 million to $175.4 million.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">For 2023, the company projects revenues in the range of $595 million to $605 million, which represents an increase of approximately 15% over 2022.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In 2022, almost 47% of Coursera&#8217;s revenue came from outside the United States, compared to 49% in 2021. And no individual country outside the US accounted for more than 10% of Coursera&#8217;s revenue.</span></p>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The Consumer segment accounted for 56% of total revenues, down from 59% in 2022. As Coursera grows, the Enterprise segment is expected to account for a larger share of total revenue. This trend is similar to that seen with Udemy, where </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/udemy-b2b-eclipses-b2c/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">B2B revenues exceeded B2C revenues</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The impact of the pandemic on Coursera&#8217;s Consumer segment is evident. In 2019, Coursera&#8217;s Consumer growth rate was only 12.6%, down from 25.4% the previous year. However, in 2020, due to the pandemic, the growth rate shot up to 59.5%.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Over the past two years, the Enterprise segment has been Coursera&#8217;s fastest-growing segment. Additionally, in 2022, the Enterprise segment grew at a rate of 50.6%, compared to 20% for the Consumer segment and -3.7% for the Degrees segment. </span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Coursera projects its lowest growth rate for 2023. The enterprise segment will grow by 20-25%, and the consumer and degrees segments by 10%. Overall growth rate may be 15%.</span></p>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Here’s how Coursera defines Segment (Consumer, Enterprise, and Degrees) Gross Margin:</span></p>
<div class="quote relative padding-horz-large xlarge-up-padding-horz-xxlarge padding-vert-xxsmall margin-bottom-large quote-pull quote-text">
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Segment gross profit represents segment revenue less content costs paid to educator partners; segment gross margin is the quotient of segment gross profit and segment revenue.</span><span class="quote_deco absolute top left height-100"> </span></p>
</div>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Over the years, Coursera&#8217;s gross and individual segment margins have been increasing. In particular, the Consumer segment experienced a significant jump in 2021 but is expected to drop again in 2023. </span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The reason for this is due to Coursera&#8217;s largest industry partner, Google, renegotiating their agreement as part of a &#8220;multi-year contract extension.&#8221; Previously, Google had been sharing a higher percentage of revenues earned from their content and certificates with Coursera. However, in 2023, Google and Coursera will switch to a &#8220;standard revenue share,&#8221; which is impacting Coursera&#8217;s margins.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Google’s first</span> <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/microcredentials/coursera-professional-certificate"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Professional Certificate</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> on Coursera, the</span> <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/google-it-support-18565"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Google IT Support Certificate</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, was announced back in 2018. But it was only in March 2021 that Google introduced three new certificates on the platform. As shown above, Coursera&#8217;s Consumer margin jumped to 66% in 2021 from 55% the prior year.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">During the earnings call, Coursera&#8217;s CFO referred to a &#8220;geography shift within the </span><a href="https://www.investopedia.com/terms/p/plstatement.asp"><span style="font-weight: 400;">P&amp;L</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">&#8221; of the company. According to my analysis, Google&#8217;s share of Coursera&#8217;s revenue could be in the proximity of $100 million.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">If you find this type of information interesting, you may want to read my in-depth analysis on how </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/coursera-google-new-deal/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Coursera&#8217;s new deal with Google could cost the company millions</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></p>
<h2><span style="font-weight: 400;">Consumer Segment</span></h2>
<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-consumer-quarterly-revenue-2020-2022.png"><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone wp-image-85670 size-full" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-consumer-quarterly-revenue-2020-2022.png" alt="Coursera: Quarterly Consumer Revenue" width="1250" height="768" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-consumer-quarterly-revenue-2020-2022.png 1250w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-consumer-quarterly-revenue-2020-2022-300x184.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-consumer-quarterly-revenue-2020-2022-1024x629.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-consumer-quarterly-revenue-2020-2022-768x472.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1250px) 100vw, 1250px" /></a></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Coursera’s consumer segments account for the majority of its revenues. In just three years, Coursera’s consumer segment revenue has grown from $32.1 million a quarter to almost $80 million a quarter. But the freemium-model also attracts learners who may later enroll in its Degrees and Enterprise segments.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In 2022 Q2, Coursera suffered a slight setback in its Consumer segment which was partially responsible for a </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/coursera-q2-2022/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">20% stock price drop</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">. According to the company’s CFO Kenneth Hahn, one of the reasons for slower than anticipated growth is: “several pricing and payment-related-tests in markets around the globe that negatively impacted consumer revenue”.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In a Class Central exclusive, we reported about</span> <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/coursera-one-time-payment/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Coursera’s pricing experiment</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">. Due to changes in credit card rules in India, the company introduced a one-time payment option for subscriptions. In our research, we found that besides India, this payment option had also been made available in Brazil.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">But according to coursera CEO Jeff Maggioncalda, when these experiments were expanded to Europe, they resulted in a revenue decline, prompting a roll back. Moving forward, Coursera will be “</span><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">ensuring a few new sign offs as we look at future experiments.</span></i><span style="font-weight: 400;">”</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">For 2023, Coursera expects the Consumer Segment to grow by 20%.</span></p>
<h2><span style="font-weight: 400;">Enterprise Segment</span></h2>
<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-enterprise-quarterly-revenue-2020-2022.png"><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85671" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-enterprise-quarterly-revenue-2020-2022.png" alt="Coursera: Quarterly Enterprise Revenue" width="1250" height="769" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-enterprise-quarterly-revenue-2020-2022.png 1250w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-enterprise-quarterly-revenue-2020-2022-300x185.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-enterprise-quarterly-revenue-2020-2022-1024x630.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-enterprise-quarterly-revenue-2020-2022-768x472.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1250px) 100vw, 1250px" /></a></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Overall, Enterprise was where Coursera showed strongest growth: a 51% year-over-year increase. The segment revenue grew from $120.4 in 2021 to $181.3 million in 2022.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Its Enterprise business consists of three segments:</span></p>
<ul>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Coursera for Campus</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Coursera for Business</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Coursera for Governments</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">For 2023, Coursera expects a growth rate of 20-25%.</span></p>
<h2><span style="font-weight: 400;">Degrees Segment</span></h2>
<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-degrees-quarterly-revenue-2019-2022.png"><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85672" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-degrees-quarterly-revenue-2019-2022.png" alt="" width="1250" height="768" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-degrees-quarterly-revenue-2019-2022.png 1250w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-degrees-quarterly-revenue-2019-2022-300x184.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-degrees-quarterly-revenue-2019-2022-1024x629.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-degrees-quarterly-revenue-2019-2022-768x472.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1250px) 100vw, 1250px" /></a></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Overall, Coursera’s degrees segment is its slowest growing segment and in 2022 it declined by 4% from $48.7 million in 2021 to $46.9 million in 2022. </span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Coursera attributed this to “</span><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">lower-than-expected student enrollments, particularly in mature U.S. and European degree programs where our revenue is concentrated today.</span></i><span style="font-weight: 400;">”</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In 2022, we saw 2 quarters of declining revenue while enrollments increased (as shown below). The reason is lower student activity — that is, students are taking fewer credit hours per semester, which effectively results in lower revenue.</span></p>
<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-degrees-quarterly-students-2019-2022.png"><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85673" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-degrees-quarterly-students-2019-2022.png" alt="" width="1250" height="769" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-degrees-quarterly-students-2019-2022.png 1250w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-degrees-quarterly-students-2019-2022-300x185.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-degrees-quarterly-students-2019-2022-1024x630.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/coursera-degrees-quarterly-students-2019-2022-768x472.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1250px) 100vw, 1250px" /></a></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">At the end of 2022, the total number of degree enrollments crossed 18,000 across its 40+ Masters and Bachelors programs.</span></p>
<h2><span style="font-weight: 400;">DeepLearning.AI Revenues</span></h2>
<div class="table">
<table>

<td></td>
<td><b>Revenue</b></td>
</tr>

<tr>

</div>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In their </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/coursera-s1-analysis/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">S-1 prospectus</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, Coursera shared how much it paid Deeplearning.AI — the company of Coursera’s co-founder and Board Member Andrew Ng — which offers courses on the platform.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In the 10–K, it refers to Deeplearning.AI as a “related party”:</span></p>
<div class="quote relative padding-horz-large xlarge-up-padding-horz-xxlarge padding-vert-xxsmall margin-bottom-large quote-pull quote-text">
<p><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">During the year ended December 31, 2017, we entered into a content sourcing agreement with a related party in the normal course of business and under standard terms. Content fees earned by the related party during the years ended December 31, 2022, 2021, and 2020 were $5,679, $6,558, and $6,171, respectively.</span></i><span class="quote_deco absolute top left height-100"> </span></p>
</div>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">These numbers are a bit different from the ones </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/coursera-s1-analysis/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Coursera disclosed in their S-1</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">. </span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The “standard terms” can be found in the </span><a href="https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1651562/000119312521071525/d65490dex1018.htm"><span style="font-weight: 400;">ONLINE COURSE HOSTING AND PLATFORM SERVICES AGREEMENT</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> between Coursera and DeepLearning.AI. To summarize, the revenue is shared 50-50.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Back in 2017, almost six years after he introduced his</span> <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/machine-learning-835"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Machine Learning class</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">,</span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/andrew-ng-deep-learning-coursera-moocs/"><span style="font-weight: 400;"> Andrew Ng announced</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> that he would launch a </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/deep-learning-18733"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Deep Learning Specialization</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">. Since then, </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/institution/deeplearning-ai"><span style="font-weight: 400;">DeepLearning.AI</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> has expanded to </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/institution/deeplearning-ai"><span style="font-weight: 400;">80+ courses and specializations</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Most notably,</span> <a href="https://www.coursera.support/s/question/0D51U00003BlVjlSAF/with-coursera-plus-subscription-unable-to-access-deeplearningai-course?language=en_US"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Deeplearning.AI courses are not part</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> of the Coursera Plus subscription. This probably means that they get a higher percentage of the revenue share.</span></p>

		<dc:creator><![CDATA[Lachin Huseynli]]></dc:creator>
		<pubDate>Tue, 07 Mar 2023 21:25:25 +0000</pubDate>
				<category><![CDATA[Reviews]]></category>

					<description><![CDATA[<p>In this FREE course by EIT Food you will learn different strategies to tackle the problem of food waste with a systematic approach.</p>
<p>The post <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/review-from-waste-to-value/">EIT Food’s Course Review: From Waste to Value &#8211; How to Tackle Food Waste</a> appeared first on <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.classcentral.com/report">The Report by Class Central</a>.</p>
]]></description>
										<content:encoded><![CDATA[<p><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85650" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/From-Waste-to-Value_-How-to-Tackle-Food-Waste-EIT-Food-Main-banner.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/From-Waste-to-Value_-How-to-Tackle-Food-Waste-EIT-Food-Main-banner.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/From-Waste-to-Value_-How-to-Tackle-Food-Waste-EIT-Food-Main-banner-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/From-Waste-to-Value_-How-to-Tackle-Food-Waste-EIT-Food-Main-banner-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></p>
<p><i>Editor’s note: This is an in-depth review of </i><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/from-waste-to-value-20611"><i>From Waste to Value: How to Tackle Food Waste</i></a><i>. This course is currently offering a free upgrade sponsored by </i><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/institution/eit-food"><i>EIT Food</i></a><i> (for one year from 6 Feb 2023). Upon completion, participants will receive a CPD accredited Learning Certificate.</i></p>
<p>I am a PhD candidate in Food Science, and I have always been driven by an obsession to comprehend and address food-related problems in a sustainable manner. However, it is obvious that the entire society must participate in order to bring the transformation that would allow future generations to live happily on our one and only home planet.</p>
<p>Food waste is one of the biggest problems that gives me the willies. Did you know that 14% of the food produced is lost before it reaches the consumers? An estimated 1.3 billion tons of food are lost or wasted annually, according to a 2011 estimate by the Food and Agriculture Organization (FAO) of the United Nations.</p>
<p>On the other hand, more than a billion people worldwide are overweight or obese, while about 820 million people are undernourished. One of the biggest paradoxes of our day is the existence of food waste and malnutrition simultaneously. Food that is wasted is a chance lost to feed the expanding global population.</p>
<p>Food waste leads to the loss of not only the food itself but also all the resources used to produce it, including land, water, labour, energy, fuel, and packaging. Additionally, methane, which is more potent than carbon dioxide at trapping heat in the atmosphere, is released when food waste is dumped in a landfill.</p>
<h2>About the course</h2>
<figure id="attachment_85651" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-85651" style="width: 1024px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img loading="lazy" class="size-full wp-image-85651" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/From-Waste-to-Value_-How-to-Tackle-Food-Waste-EIT-Food-Week-1-Case-study_-RethinkResource.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/From-Waste-to-Value_-How-to-Tackle-Food-Waste-EIT-Food-Week-1-Case-study_-RethinkResource.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/From-Waste-to-Value_-How-to-Tackle-Food-Waste-EIT-Food-Week-1-Case-study_-RethinkResource-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/From-Waste-to-Value_-How-to-Tackle-Food-Waste-EIT-Food-Week-1-Case-study_-RethinkResource-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-85651" class="wp-caption-text">From Week 1, Case Study RethinkResource</figcaption></figure>
<p>Those enormous current food waste challenges were the main reason I took the course called <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/from-waste-to-value-20611">From Waste to Value: How to Tackle Food Waste</a> by <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/institution/eit-food">EIT Food</a> to see the current development. Additionally, I was looking forward to understanding a deeper cause of food waste, its effects on climate change, and different ways to prevent it in the first place.</p>
<figure id="attachment_85652" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-85652" style="width: 1024px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img loading="lazy" class="size-full wp-image-85652" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/From-Waste-to-Value_-How-to-Tackle-Food-Waste-EIT-Food-Week-2-A-holistic-approach-to-food.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/From-Waste-to-Value_-How-to-Tackle-Food-Waste-EIT-Food-Week-2-A-holistic-approach-to-food.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/From-Waste-to-Value_-How-to-Tackle-Food-Waste-EIT-Food-Week-2-A-holistic-approach-to-food-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/From-Waste-to-Value_-How-to-Tackle-Food-Waste-EIT-Food-Week-2-A-holistic-approach-to-food-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-85652" class="wp-caption-text">From week 2, &#8220;A holistic Approach to food&#8221;.</figcaption></figure>
<p>I can honestly point out that course covered it all! Even more! They mention the <a href="https://www.futurelearn.com/info/courses/from-waste-to-value/0/steps/168418">Food Use Hierarchy</a>, why it is necessary to shift the focus towards keeping food in the food chain for as long as possible, and using circular economy to tackle the solution was a nice systematic approach. I was thrilled to see new technological ideas to contribute to the solution of food waste, especially through smart packaging. I really value the fact that this online course is creating a huge awareness of the problem and providing simple solutions to avoid them as individuals. Simple steps such as making a grocery list to amazing unique recipes to diminish food waste.</p>
<h2>Time commitment</h2>
<figure id="attachment_85653" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-85653" style="width: 1024px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img loading="lazy" class="size-full wp-image-85653" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/From-Waste-to-Value_-How-to-Tackle-Food-Waste-EIT-Food-Week-3-Agents-of-change-retailers.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/From-Waste-to-Value_-How-to-Tackle-Food-Waste-EIT-Food-Week-3-Agents-of-change-retailers.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/From-Waste-to-Value_-How-to-Tackle-Food-Waste-EIT-Food-Week-3-Agents-of-change-retailers-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/From-Waste-to-Value_-How-to-Tackle-Food-Waste-EIT-Food-Week-3-Agents-of-change-retailers-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-85653" class="wp-caption-text">From week 3, &#8220;Agents of change &#8211; retailers&#8221;.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The best part about the course is that it is only 3 weeks long and doesn’t require more of your time daily. You are free to follow the course according to your own schedule, and all the course materials can easily be downloaded. With less patience and huge curiosity, I finished the course in a week and successfully passed the quiz.</p>
<h2>Conclusion</h2>
<p>It is always nice to see small achievements when they are compemented with a certificate, which, in this case, it was. If you are looking forward to widening your knowledge of the importance of food waste issues, this course is your call!</p>
<figure id="attachment_85654" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-85654" style="width: 737px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img loading="lazy" class="size-full wp-image-85654" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/Lachin-Huseynli-from-waste-to-value_certificate_of_achievement.png" alt="" width="737" height="1043" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/Lachin-Huseynli-from-waste-to-value_certificate_of_achievement.png 737w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/Lachin-Huseynli-from-waste-to-value_certificate_of_achievement-212x300.png 212w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/Lachin-Huseynli-from-waste-to-value_certificate_of_achievement-724x1024.png 724w" sizes="(max-width: 737px) 100vw, 737px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-85654" class="wp-caption-text">My certificate of achievement.</figcaption></figure>
<h2>What’s next</h2>
<p>Well, it wasn’t the end. I have taken several courses produced by EIT Food and am currently following <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/future-food-15148">Future Food: Sustainable Food Systems for the 21st Century</a> and <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/how-is-my-food-made-14494">How Food is Made: Understanding Food Processing Technologies</a>. They are also impressive!</p>

<h2><span style="font-weight: 400;">What is Bookkeeping?</span></h2>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Bookkeeping is the practice of recording the financial information of an individual or a business, and is part of the </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/subject/accounting" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">accounting</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> process. Day-to-day financial transactions such as revenue, taxes, interest, loans and others can be recorded and stored, and the accuracy and efficiency of documentation determines the overall financial health of the organization.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Bookkeeper is the person designated by an organization to perform bookkeeping functions. Research shows that methods of keeping accounts have existed as far back in history as </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bookkeeping#History" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">2600 BCE</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> when Babylonians used to write records on clay slabs. However, most businesses today use computer-based methods for bookkeeping such as a simple spreadsheet or more advanced software.</span></p>
<h3><span style="font-weight: 400;">Why are Bookkeeping Skills Important?</span></h3>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The job market for bookkeepers is expected to grow with the rise of small businesses and the increasing importance of financial management. Bookkeepers with strong technical skills, including cloud computing and automation, are in high demand and can offer additional value through data analysis.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Bookkeeper salaries vary greatly by country, location, and company size. </span><a href="https://www.bls.gov/ooh/office-and-administrative-support/bookkeeping-accounting-and-auditing-clerks.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">In the US</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, the median hourly wage is $20.66, and </span><a href="https://uk.indeed.com/career/bookkeeper/salaries/England" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">in the UK</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, the average salary is £25,000. In Canada, the average salary ranges from $40,000 to $60,000, while </span><a href="https://au.indeed.com/career/bookkeeper/salaries" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">in Australia</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, it ranges from $50,000 to $70,000. </span><a href="https://nz.indeed.com/career/bookkeeper/salaries" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">In New Zealand</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, the average salary is NZD 50,000. Salaries may vary based on job responsibilities, experience and location.</span></p>
<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone wp-image-79248 size-full" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Class-Central-Preview-2.png" alt="Find your next course on Class Central" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Class-Central-Preview-2.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Class-Central-Preview-2-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/Class-Central-Preview-2-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a></p>
<h2><span style="font-weight: 400;">Course Ranking Methodology</span></h2>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">I built this ranking following the now tried-and-tested methodology I used in previous rankings (</span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/category/best-courses/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">you can find them all here</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">). It involves a three-step process:</span></p>
<ol>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><b>Research:</b><span style="font-weight: 400;"> I started by leveraging Class Central’s database with </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/subjects" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">100K online courses</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> and 200K+ reviews. Then, I made a preliminary selection of </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/search?q=bookkeeping" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">145+ bookkeeping courses</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> by rating, reviews, and bookmarks.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><b>Evaluate:</b><span style="font-weight: 400;"> I read through reviews on Class Central, Reddit, and course providers to understand what other learners thought about each course and combined it with my own experience as a </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/@archisha" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">learner</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><b>Select:</b><span style="font-weight: 400;"> Well-made courses were picked if they presented valuable and engaging content and they have to fit in a set of criteria and be ranked accordingly: comprehensive curriculum, release date, affordability, ratings and enrollments.</span></li>
</ol>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The end result is a unique selection of courses that combines a decade of Class Central data and my own experience as an online learner to try to get the best of both worlds. So far, I’ve spent more than 12 hours building this list, and I’ll continue to update it.</span></p>

<h2 id="anchor-1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">1. Bookkeeping Foundations and Advanced Techniques (LinkedIn Learning)</span></h2>
<figure id="attachment_85631" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-85631" style="width: 1024px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img loading="lazy" class="size-full wp-image-85631" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/1.-Bookkeeping-Foundations-and-Advanced-Techniques-LinkedIn-Learning.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/1.-Bookkeeping-Foundations-and-Advanced-Techniques-LinkedIn-Learning.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/1.-Bookkeeping-Foundations-and-Advanced-Techniques-LinkedIn-Learning-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/1.-Bookkeeping-Foundations-and-Advanced-Techniques-LinkedIn-Learning-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-85631" class="wp-caption-text">Jim Stice (left) and Kay Stice (right), instructors</figcaption></figure>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">My first pick for the best bookkeeping online course is a collection of two courses offered by Jim Stice and Kay Stice on LinkedIn Learning.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The two courses you’ll be taking are:</span></p>
<ol>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/linkedin-learning-accounting-foundations-bookkeeping-29344" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Accounting Foundations: Bookkeeping</span></a></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/linkedin-learning-advanced-bookkeeping-techniques-101372" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Advanced Bookkeeping Techniques</span></a></li>
</ol>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The first course teaches the basics of bookkeeping and financial statement creation while the second course focuses on advanced accounting strategies for managing financial entries. After completing both the courses, you’ll have developed the essential skills and knowledge needed to effectively manage the financial records of a business or organization.</span></p>
<h3><span style="font-weight: 400;">What You’ll Learn</span></h3>
<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/linkedin-learning-accounting-foundations-bookkeeping-29344" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Accounting Foundations: Bookkeeping</span></a></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In the course, you&#8217;ll learn about financial statements, which includes the balance sheet, income statement, and statement of cash flows. You&#8217;ll also learn about the four steps in the bookkeeping process: routine bookkeeping, analyzing transactions, using accounts to categorize transactions, and exercising caution with revenues, expenses, and dividends.</span></p>
<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/linkedin-learning-advanced-bookkeeping-techniques-101372" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Advanced Bookkeeping Techniques</span></a></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">This course covers debits and credits, journal entries, adjusting entries, closing entries, and correcting errors. You&#8217;ll explore journal entries for receiving financing, buying assets, and recording revenues and expenses. Finally, you’ll learn about closing entries and correcting errors.</span></p>
<h3><span style="font-weight: 400;">How You’ll Learn</span></h3>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The first course is broken down into 6 modules and the second course is broken down into 7 modules. Each course involves about 1 to 2 hours of work. Concepts are taught through a combination of videos, practice exercises and quizzes.</span></p>

<h2 id="anchor-2"><span style="font-weight: 400;">2. Introduction to Bookkeeping (ACCA)</span></h2>
<figure id="attachment_85639" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-85639" style="width: 1024px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img loading="lazy" class="size-full wp-image-85639" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/2.-Introduction-to-Bookkeeping-ACCA.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/2.-Introduction-to-Bookkeeping-ACCA.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/2.-Introduction-to-Bookkeeping-ACCA-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/2.-Introduction-to-Bookkeeping-ACCA-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-85639" class="wp-caption-text">Malvi Shah, instructor</figcaption></figure>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The two courses you&#8217;ll be taking are:</span></p>
<ol>

<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/edx-intermediate-bookkeeping-8881" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Intermediate Bookkeeping</span></a></li>
</ol>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">After completing both courses, you will be able to start a career in business, finance or accountancy, study business or finance, launch your own start-up, and prepare for the ACCA exams in Recording Financial Transactions (FA1) and Maintaining Financial Records (FA2).</span></p>
<h3><span style="font-weight: 400;">What You’ll Learn</span></h3>
<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/edx-introduction-to-bookkeeping-8882" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Introduction to Bookkeeping</span></a></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In this course, you&#8217;ll learn about business transactions and documentation, including the duality of transactions and the double entry system, the banking process and transactions, payroll, ledger accounts, sales and purchases credit transactions, reconciliations, and the trial balance.</span></p>
<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/edx-intermediate-bookkeeping-8881" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Intermediate Bookkeeping</span></a></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In this course, you&#8217;ll learn about generally accepted accounting principles and concepts, the principles and process of bookkeeping, preparing journal entries, recording transactions and events, extending the trial balance, and accounting for partnerships. You’ll also cover preparing the trial balance and correcting errors.</span></p>
<h3><span style="font-weight: 400;">How You’ll Learn</span></h3>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Both the courses are broken down into 6 weeks. Each week involves about 5 to 8 hours of work. Concepts are taught through a combination of videos, readings and quizzes.</span></p>

</ol>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">After completing all three courses, you will have a comprehensive understanding of bookkeeping fundamentals, including debits, credits, the accounting equation, analyzing and recording transactions, as well as end-of-the-month and end-of-the-year closing entries, depreciation, prepaid items, accrued payroll, inventory and QuickBooks.</span></p>
<h3><span style="font-weight: 400;">What You’ll Learn</span></h3>
<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/udemy-bookkeeping-basics-25586" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Bookkeeping Basics #1: Understand the Fundamentals</span></a></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">This course will teach you the key principles of financial management, including setting financial goals, creating a budget, managing cash flow, and understanding financial statements. You&#8217;ll also learn about different sources of funding, such as loans and investors, and the importance of managing risk.</span></p>
<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/udemy-bb2-mechanics-87030" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Bookkeeping Basics #2: Understand The Mechanics</span></a></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In this course, you&#8217;ll learn about the Fundamental Accounting Equation, bookkeeping accounts, balancing T-accounts/ledgers, Accounting Cycle&#8217;s steps, Interim and Final financial reports, Adjusting and Closing activities. You&#8217;ll also learn how to record adjusting entries and why annual bookkeeping records are closed each year.</span></p>
<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/udemy-bb3-qbfundamentals-121505" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Bookkeeping Basics #3: QuickBooks<img src="https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/13.1.0/72x72/2122.png" alt="™" class="wp-smiley" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" /> Desktop Fundamentals</span></a></p>

You&#8217;ll also explore the differences between QB Desktop and QB Online.</span></p>

<h3><span style="font-weight: 400;">What You’ll Learn</span></h3>

<h2 id="anchor-10"><span style="font-weight: 400;">10. </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/bookkeeping-basics-46031" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Bookkeeping Basics (Intuit Professional Development)</span></a></h2>
<figure id="attachment_85638" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-85638" style="width: 1024px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img loading="lazy" class="size-full wp-image-85638" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/10.-Bookkeeping-Basics-Intuit.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/10.-Bookkeeping-Basics-Intuit.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/10.-Bookkeeping-Basics-Intuit-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/10.-Bookkeeping-Basics-Intuit-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-85638" class="wp-caption-text">What you’ll learn</figcaption></figure>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">My tenth pick for the best bookkeeping online course is the </span><b>free-to-audit</b> <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/course/bookkeeping-basics-46031" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">Bookkeeping Basics</span></i></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, offered by Intuit Professional Development on Coursera.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">This course will teach you all about the role of a bookkeeper and the essential accounting concepts needed to read and create financial statements. After completing this course, you will be able to define accounting, summarize the double entry accounting method and explain the ethical and social responsibilities of bookkeepers in maintaining financial integrity. This course is suitable for anyone interested in bookkeeping, regardless of previous experience.</span></p>
<h3><span style="font-weight: 400;">What You’ll Learn</span></h3>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">This course covers the basics of accounting, starting with an introduction to the role of a bookkeeper and the accounting equation. You&#8217;ll learn how bookkeepers use the general journal and general ledger to record and keep track of business transactions, as well as how to create trial balances and produce financial statements using accounting software.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">You’ll then delve into accounting principles and practices, including key assumptions and principles and the different types of accounting methods bookkeepers use. By the end of this course, you&#8217;ll have a solid understanding of accounting concepts and measurement, the accounting cycle, and accounting principles and practices.</span></p>
<h3><span style="font-weight: 400;">How You’ll Learn</span></h3>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The course is broken down into 4 modules. Each module involves about 30 to 50 minutes of work. Concepts are taught through a combination of videos, readings and quizzes.</span></p>

		<title>FutureLearn&#8217;s Turbulent Year Culminates in Price Hike as CEO Departs</title>
		<link>https://www.classcentral.com/report/futurelearn-price-hike-ceo-exit/</link>
					<comments>https://www.classcentral.com/report/futurelearn-price-hike-ceo-exit/#comments</comments>
		
		<dc:creator><![CDATA[Manoel Cortes Mendez]]></dc:creator>
		<pubDate>Tue, 07 Mar 2023 11:53:46 +0000</pubDate>
				<category><![CDATA[News]]></category>
		<category><![CDATA[Coursera]]></category>
		<category><![CDATA[Futurelearn]]></category>
		<guid isPermaLink="false">https://www.classcentral.com/report/?p=85614</guid>

					<description><![CDATA[<p>FutureLearn’s subscription plan is now comparable in price to Coursera’s, but it doesn’t offer nearly as much.</p>
<p>The post <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/futurelearn-price-hike-ceo-exit/">FutureLearn&#8217;s Turbulent Year Culminates in Price Hike as CEO Departs</a> appeared first on <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.classcentral.com/report">The Report by Class Central</a>.</p>
]]></description>
										<content:encoded><![CDATA[<p><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/futurelearn-raises-sub-price.png"><img loading="lazy" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-85616" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/futurelearn-raises-sub-price.png" alt="" width="1024" height="512" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/futurelearn-raises-sub-price.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/futurelearn-raises-sub-price-300x150.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/futurelearn-raises-sub-price-768x384.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">FutureLearn, Europe’s main counterpart to Coursera and edX, has increased the price of </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/futurelearn-unlimited/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Unlimited</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, its catalog subscription plan.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The price hike follows another monetization move by FutureLearn’s new leadership: in January, </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/futurelearn-expands-paywall/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">FutureLearn expanded its paywall</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, as exclusively reported by </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Class Central</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">I was surprised by this price hike. The cost of FutureLearn’s subscription is now comparable to Coursera’s. But Coursera has a significantly larger (and in my view, more attractive) catalog.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">This is the latest development in FutureLearn’s tumultuous year, which was punctuated by funding troubles, leadership changes, and layoffs.</span></p>
<h2><span style="font-weight: 400;">Price Hike</span></h2>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">On March 1st, we learned in an email that, effective immediately, FutureLearn would increase the cost of Unlimited, its subscription plan, which gives access to two-thirds of the courses offered on the platform.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Here are the old and new prices of FutureLearn Unlimited in different regions:</span></p>
<div class="table">
<table>
<caption style="caption-side: bottom;"><span style="font-weight: 400;">FutureLearn Unlimited annual price per region</span></caption>
<thead>
<tr>
<td></td>
<td><b>Old Price</b></td>
<td><b>New Price</b></td>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><b>US</b></td>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400;">US $279.99</span></td>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400;">US $349.99</span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>EU</b></td>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400;">€249.99</span></td>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400;">€299.99</span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>UK</b></td>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400;">£199.99</span></td>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400;">£249.99</span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>Australia</b></td>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400;">AU $379.99</span></td>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400;">AU $479.99</span></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</div>
<h2><span style="font-weight: 400;">Tailing Coursera</span></h2>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The price increase surprised my Class Central colleagues and me, since it puts the cost of FutureLearn’s subscription in the same ballpark as that of Coursera’s — Coursera Plus costs $399 per year.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">FutureLearn’s subscription predates Coursera’s, and it launched at a significantly lower price:</span></p>
<ul>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/futurelearn-unlimited/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">FutureLearn Unlimited</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> launched in March 2019 and cost $199 per year.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/coursera-plus-launch/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Coursera Plus</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> launched in February 2020 and cost $399 per year.</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The issue with FutureLearn’s price increase is that Coursera’s subscription plan:</span></p>
<ul>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Boasts a significantly larger catalog.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Includes better-known partners, such as <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/institution/google">Google</a>, <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/university/yale">Yale</a>, and <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/university/jhu">Johns Hopkins</a>.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Extends to microcredentials — Specializations and Professional Certificates.</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Here’s a brief comparison of both subscription plans:</span></p>
<div class="table">
<table>
<caption style="caption-side: bottom;"><span style="font-weight: 400;">By the Numbers: FutureLearn vs Coursera subscription plan</span></caption>
<thead>
<tr>

<td><b>FutureLearn Unlimited</b></td>
<td><b>Coursera Plus</b></td>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><b>Courses included</b></td>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400;">1379 (68% of courses)</span></td>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400;">6526 (96% of courses)</span></td>
</tr>
<tr>

<td><span style="font-weight: 400;">None</span></td>
<td>
<ul>

</ul>

</tr>
<tr>

</table>

<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">(For a broader comparison of FutureLearn and Coursera, read our end-of-year analysis: </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/2022-year-in-review/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">2022 Year in Review: The “New Normal” that Wasn&#8217;t</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.)</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In light of the numbers above, I would imagine most learners would rather pay an extra $50 to have access to Coursera’s catalog for a year.</span></p>
<figure id="attachment_85624" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-85624" style="width: 1514px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/futurelearn-vs-coursera-discount-final.png"><img loading="lazy" class="wp-image-85624 size-full" src="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/futurelearn-vs-coursera-discount-final.png" alt="" width="1514" height="486" srcset="https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/futurelearn-vs-coursera-discount-final.png 1514w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/futurelearn-vs-coursera-discount-final-300x96.png 300w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/futurelearn-vs-coursera-discount-final-1024x329.png 1024w, https://www.classcentral.com/report/wp-content/uploads/2023/03/futurelearn-vs-coursera-discount-final-768x247.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 1514px) 100vw, 1514px" /></a><figcaption id="caption-attachment-85624" class="wp-caption-text">New Year’s discount: on the left, FutureLearn’s 30% (image courtesy my Australian colleague <a href="https://www.classcentral.com/@pat">Pat</a>, so the price is in AU$); on the right, Coursera’s 50% (price in US$).</figcaption></figure>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Even when it comes to discounts, Coursera recently proved more competitive. Both companies started the year with sales that lasted a month or more, but Coursera discounted its subscription by 50%, while FutureLearn only discounted it by 30%, as you can see above.</span></p>
<h2><span style="font-weight: 400;">Signs of Turmoil</span></h2>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">FutureLearn’s price increase is the culmination of a difficult year at the company, as reflected by our coverage of the platform:</span></p>
<ul>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><b>Aug 2022</b><span style="font-weight: 400;">: </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/futurelearn-funding-pains/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">FutureLearn requires extra funding to survive</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><b>Nov 2022</b><span style="font-weight: 400;">: </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/futurelearn-layoffs/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">FutureLearn conducts layoffs</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><b>Dec 2022</b><span style="font-weight: 400;">: </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/gus-acquires-futurelearn/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">FutureLearn gets acquired by GUS</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><b>Jan 2023</b><span style="font-weight: 400;">: </span><a href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/futurelearn-expands-paywall/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">FutureLearn expands paywall</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></li>
</ul>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">And just yesterday, we learned that FutureLearn CEO </span><a href="https://www.timeshighereducation.com/news/futurelearn-chief-executive-andy-hancock-exits-after-gus-takeover"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Andy Hancock would be leaving the company</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> at the end of the month.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The price of a subscription plan is expected to increase over time. But the fact that this increase comes in the wake of a stream of signs of turmoil at FutureLearn suggests to me that the decision may stem from urgency rather from a sound pricing strategy.</span></p>
<p>The post <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.classcentral.com/report/futurelearn-price-hike-ceo-exit/">FutureLearn&#8217;s Turbulent Year Culminates in Price Hike as CEO Departs</a> appeared first on <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.classcentral.com/report">The Report by Class Central</a>.</p>
